   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Geographic coordinate conversion
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Geodesy" title="Geodesy">
        geodesy
       </a>
       ,
       <b>
        conversion
       </b>
       among different
       <b>
        geographic coordinate
       </b>
       systems is made necessary by the different
       <a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">
        geographic coordinate systems
       </a>
       in use across the world and over time. Coordinate conversion is composed of a number of different types of conversion: format change of geographic coordinates, conversion of coordinate systems, or transformation to different
       <a href="/wiki/Geodetic_datum" title="Geodetic datum">
        geodetic datums
       </a>
       . Geographic coordinate conversion has applications in
       <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">
        cartography
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Surveying" title="Surveying">
        surveying
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Navigation" title="Navigation">
        navigation
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographic_information_systems" title="Geographic information systems">
        geographic information systems
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In geodesy, geographic coordinate
       <i>
        conversion
       </i>
       is defined as translation among different coordinate formats or
       <a href="/wiki/Map_projection" title="Map projection">
        map projections
       </a>
       all referenced to the same geodetic datum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster2009_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Foster2009-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A geographic coordinate
       <i>
        transformation
       </i>
       is a translation among different geodetic datums. Both geographic coordinate conversion and transformation will be considered in this article.
      </p>
      <p>
       This article assumes readers are already familiar with the content in the articles
       <a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">
        geographic coordinate system
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Geodetic_datum" title="Geodetic datum">
        geodetic datum
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coordinate_format_conversion">
        Coordinate format conversion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Coordinate format conversion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Informally, specifying a geographic location usually means giving the location's
       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
        latitude
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">
        longitude
       </a>
       . The numerical values for latitude and longitude can occur in a number of different formats:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Degree_(angle)" title="Degree (angle)">
         degrees
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minute_of_arc" title="Minute of arc">
         minutes
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arcsecond" title="Arcsecond">
         seconds
        </a>
        : 40° 26′ 46″ N 79° 58′ 56″ W
       </li>
       <li>
        degrees decimal minutes: 40° 26.767′ N 79° 58.933′ W
       </li>
       <li>
        decimal degrees: 40.446° N 79.982° W
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       There are 60 minutes in a degree and 60 seconds in a minute. Therefore, to convert from a degrees minutes seconds format to a decimal degrees format, one may use the formula
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\rm {{decimal\ degrees}={\rm {{degrees}+{\rm {{minutes}/60+{\rm {{seconds}/3600}}}}}}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                 </mi>

                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 =
                </mo>

                  </mo>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                     </mo>

                     60

                    </mo>

                       <mo>
                        /
                       </mo>
                      </mrow>
                      <mn>
                       3600
                      </mn>
                     </mrow>
                    </mrow>
                   </mrow>
                  </mrow>
                 </mrow>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\rm {{decimal\ degrees}={\rm {{degrees}+{\rm {{minutes}/60+{\rm {{seconds}/3600}}}}}}}}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\rm {{decimal\ degrees}={\rm {{degrees}+{\rm {{minutes}/60+{\rm {{seconds}/3600}}}}}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dab9be0085459b7f700c0ce1e9457a5776556b97" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:56.835ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
        .
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       To convert back from decimal degree format to degrees minutes seconds format,
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\rm {degrees}}&amp;=\lfloor {\rm {{decimal\ degrees}\rfloor }}\\{\rm {minutes}}&amp;=\lfloor 60\times ({\rm {{decimal\ degrees}-{\rm {{degrees})\rfloor }}}}\\{\rm {seconds}}&amp;=3600\times ({\rm {{decimal\ degrees}-{\rm {{degrees})-60\times {\rm {minutes}}}}}}\\\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt">
                <mtr>
                 <mtd>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     d
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     e
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     g
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     r
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     e
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     e
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     s
                    </mi>
                   </mrow>
                  </mrow>
                 </mtd>
                 <mtd>
                  <mi>
                  </mi>
                  <mo>
                   =
                  </mo>
                  <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">

      <p>
       where the notation
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \lfloor x\rfloor }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

         </math>
        </span>

       </span>
       means take the integer part of
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

       </span>
       and is called a
       <a href="/wiki/Floor_and_ceiling_functions" title="Floor and ceiling functions">
        floor function
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coordinate_system_conversion">
        Coordinate system conversion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Coordinate system conversion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       A coordinate system conversion is a conversion from one coordinate system to another, with both coordinate systems based on the same geodetic datum. Common conversion tasks include conversion between geodetic and
       <a href="/wiki/ECEF" title="ECEF">
        ECEF
       </a>
       coordinates and conversion from one type of map projection to another.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="From_geodetic_to_ECEF_coordinates">
        From geodetic to
        <a href="/wiki/ECEF" title="ECEF">
         ECEF
        </a>
        coordinates
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: From geodetic to ECEF coordinates">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg/220px-Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg/330px-Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg/440px-Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>

         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geodetic_latitude_and_the_length_of_Normal.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>

         The length PQ is called
         <i>
          Normal
         </i>
         (
         <span class="mwe-math-element">
          <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

         </span>
         ). The length IQ is equal to
         <span class="mwe-math-element">

         </span>
         . R =
         <span class="mwe-math-element">

      <p>
       Geodetic coordinates (latitude
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ \phi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

       <span class="mwe-math-element">

       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

       </span>
       ) can be converted into
       <a href="/wiki/ECEF" title="ECEF">
        ECEF
       </a>
       coordinates using the following formulae:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gps-chap10_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gps-chap10-3">

       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

       and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">

       </span>
       are the equatorial radius (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-major_axis" title="Semi-major axis">

       ) and the polar radius (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-minor_axis" title="Semi-minor axis">
        semi-minor axis
       </a>
       ), respectively. The
       <i>
        normal
       </i>
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \,N(\phi )}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

              (
             </mo>
             <mi>
              ϕ
              <!-- ϕ -->
             </mi>
             <mo stretchy="false">

       </span>
       is the distance from the surface to the Z-axis along the ellipsoid normal (see "
       <a href="/wiki/Earth_radius#Radius_of_curvature" title="Earth radius">
        Radius of curvature on the Earth
       </a>
       "). The parameter

        </span>

       so the following equation holds:

        </span>

      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle p={\sqrt {X^{2}+Y^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

               </mo>

       </span>
       and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle e^{2}=1-{\frac {b^{2}}{a^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

             </msup>
             <mo>

             </mo>

             </mn>
             <mo>

              <!-- − -->
             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

            {\displaystyle e^{2}=1-{\frac {b^{2}}{a^{2}}}}

        </span>
        <img alt="{\displaystyle e^{2}=1-{\frac {b^{2}}{a^{2}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a74130b944efd8b9342c2e12bb8823dd53013086" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:12.359ex; height:6.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the square of the first numerical eccentricity of the ellipsoid.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Orthogonal_coordinates" title="Orthogonal coordinates">
        orthogonality
       </a>
       of the coordinates is confirmed via differentiation:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\begin{pmatrix}dX\\dY\\dZ\\\end{pmatrix}}&amp;={\begin{pmatrix}-\sin \lambda &amp;-\sin \phi \cos \lambda &amp;\cos \phi \cos \lambda \\\cos \lambda &amp;-\sin \phi \sin \lambda &amp;\cos \phi \sin \lambda \\0&amp;\cos \phi &amp;\sin \phi \\\end{pmatrix}}{\begin{pmatrix}dE\\dN\\dU\\\end{pmatrix}},\\{\begin{pmatrix}dE\\dN\\dU\\\end{pmatrix}}&amp;={\begin{pmatrix}\left(N(\phi )+h\right)\cos \phi &amp;0&amp;0\\0&amp;M(\phi )+h&amp;0\\0&amp;0&amp;1\\\end{pmatrix}}{\begin{pmatrix}d\lambda \\d\phi \\dh\\\end{pmatrix}},\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt">
                <mtr>
                 <mtd>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mrow>
                    <mo>
                     (
                    </mo>
                    <mtable columnspacing="1em" rowspacing="4pt">
                     <mtr>
                      <mtd>
                       <mi>
                        d
                       </mi>
                       <mi>
                        X
                       </mi>
                      </mtd>
                     </mtr>
                     <mtr>
                      <mtd>
                       <mi>
                        d
                       </mi>
                       <mi>
                        Y
                       </mi>
                      </mtd>
                     </mtr>
                     <mtr>
                      <mtd>
                       <mi>
                        d
                       </mi>
                       <mi>
                        Z
                       </mi>
                      </mtd>
                     </mtr>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="From_ECEF_to_geodetic_coordinates">
        From ECEF to geodetic coordinates
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: From ECEF to geodetic coordinates">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The conversion of ECEF coordinates to geodetic coordinates (such WGS84) involves more trigonometry but is sensitive to small accuracy due to Rn and h being maybe 10^6 apart,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but longitude is same as geocentric,
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \,\lambda }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mspace width="thinmathspace">
             </mspace>
             <mi>
              λ
              <!-- λ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \,\lambda }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\,\lambda " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a4fb547bf232593dc98e480402a274f1746d8a4a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.742ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There are several methods that solve the equation; two are shown.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Newton.E2.80.93Raphson_method">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Newton–Raphson_method">
        Newton–Raphson method
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Newton–Raphson method">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The following Bowring's irrational geodetic-latitude equation
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is efficient to be solved by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newton%E2%80%93Raphson" title="Newton–Raphson">
        Newton–Raphson
       </a>
       iteration method:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \kappa -1-{\frac {e^{2}a\kappa }{\sqrt {p^{2}+(1-e^{2})Z^{2}\kappa ^{2}}}}=0,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               κ
               <!-- κ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mn>
               1
              </mn>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <msup>
                  <mi>
                   e
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    2
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msup>
                 <mi>
                  a
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  κ
                  <!-- κ -->
                 </mi>
                </mrow>

                 <msup>
                  <mi>
                   p

                 </mo>

                 </mo>

                  <!-- − -->
                 </mo>

                  <mi>

                 </mo>

                  </mi>

                  </mrow>

                  </mi>

                </msqrt>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               0
              </mn>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \kappa -1-{\frac {e^{2}a\kappa }{\sqrt {p^{2}+(1-e^{2})Z^{2}\kappa ^{2}}}}=0,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle \kappa -1-{\frac {e^{2}a\kappa }{\sqrt {p^{2}+(1-e^{2})Z^{2}\kappa ^{2}}}}=0,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f378937485ba71868d153a5f6504c16b4412778c" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:34.42ex; height:7.009ex;"/>
        </span>

      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \kappa ={\frac {p}{Z}}\tan \phi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

             </mi>

           </annotation>

        <img alt="{\displaystyle \kappa ={\frac {p}{Z}}\tan \phi }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ddbcd6a0346cc44d07cca9808aff23c7c9a2cf20" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:12.473ex; height:4.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       . The height is calculated as:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle h=e^{-2}(\kappa ^{-1}-{\kappa _{0}}^{-1}){\sqrt {p^{2}+Z^{2}\kappa ^{2}}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               h
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                e
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                κ
                <!-- κ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  κ
                  <!-- κ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   0
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <msqrt>
                <msup>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>

       The constant
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \,\kappa _{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

       </span>
       is a good starter value for the iteration when
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle h\approx 0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

              <!-- ≈ -->
             </mo>
             <mn>
              0
             </mn>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle h\approx 0}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="h\approx 0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c6bb393202ea6edfd065df1cd2c3178245569bf6" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.6ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       . Bowring showed that the single iteration produces a sufficiently accurate solution. He used extra trigonometric functions in his original formulation.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Ferrari.27s_solution">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ferrari's_solution">
        Ferrari's solution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ferrari's solution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The quartic equation of
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \kappa }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              κ
              <!-- κ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \kappa }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\kappa " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54ddec2e922c5caea4e47d04feef86e782dc8e6d" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.339ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       , derived from the above, can be solved by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quartic_equation#Ferrari.27s_solution" title="Quartic equation">
        Ferrari's solution
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>

         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>

      <h5>
       <span id="The_application_of_Ferrari.27s_solution">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_application_of_Ferrari's_solution">
        The application of Ferrari's solution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The application of Ferrari's solution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       A number of techniques and algorithms are available but the most accurate according to Zhu,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is the following 15 step procedure summarised by Kaplan. It is assumed that geodetic parameters
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a,b,e,e'\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              {
             </mo>
             <mi>
              a
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>
              b
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>
              e
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msup>
              <mi>
               e
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ′
              </mo>
             </msup>
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              }
             </mo>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \{a,b,e,e'\}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\{a,b,e,e'\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/527aa8ac1f8cf7f9cc69e4db63736d1c8b9ed9f2" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.506ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       are known
      </p>

       <dd>

      <h3>
       <span id="Geodetic_to.2Ffrom_ENU_coordinates">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geodetic_to/from_ENU_coordinates">
        Geodetic to/from
        <a href="/wiki/Axes_conventions#Ground_reference_frames:_ENU_and_NED" title="Axes conventions">
         ENU
        </a>
        coordinates
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geodetic to/from ENU coordinates">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       To convert from geodetic coordinates to local
       <a href="/wiki/Axes_conventions#Ground_reference_frames:_ENU_and_NED" title="Axes conventions">
        ENU
       </a>
       coordinates is a two-stage process:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Convert geodetic coordinates to ECEF coordinates
       </li>
       <li>
        Convert ECEF coordinates to local ENU coordinates
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       To convert from local ENU coordinates to geodetic coordinates is a two-stage process
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Convert local ENU coordinates to ECEF coordinates
       </li>
       <li>
        Convert ECEF coordinates to geodetic coordinates
       </li>
      </ol>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="From_ECEF_to_ENU">
        From ECEF to ENU
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: From ECEF to ENU">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       To transform from ECEF coordinates to the local coordinates we need a local reference point, typically this might be the location of a radar. If a radar is located at
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \{X_{r},Y_{r},Z_{r}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

             </mo>

               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>

             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               Z
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

               </mi>
              </mrow>

             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              }

            {\displaystyle \{X_{r},Y_{r},Z_{r}\}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>

        </span>

       </span>
       and an aircraft at
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

       <b>
        Note:
       </b>
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ \phi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

       </span>
       is the
       <i>
        geodetic
       </i>
       latitude. A prior version of this page showed use of the
       <i>
        geocentric
       </i>
       latitude (
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ \phi ^{\prime }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mtext>
             </mtext>

              <mi>
               ϕ
               <!-- ϕ -->
              </mi>

                ′
                <!-- ′ -->
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msup>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \ \phi ^{\prime }}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\ \phi ^{\prime }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/02fb387a76a6bc1b55fb2076c1e04c70159ef505" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.651ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       ). The
       <i>
        geocentric
       </i>
       latitude is
       <i>
        not
       </i>
       the appropriate
       <i>
        up
       </i>
       direction for the local tangent plane. If the original
       <i>
        geodetic
       </i>
       latitude is available it should be used, otherwise, the relationship between
       <i>
        geodetic
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        geocentric
       </i>
       latitude has an altitude dependency, and is captured by:
      </p>

         <img alt="\tan \phi ^{\prime }={\frac {Z_{r}}{\sqrt {X_{r}^{2}+Y_{r}^{2}}}}={\frac {N(\phi )(1-f)^{2}+h}{N(\phi )+h}}\tan \phi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f6594168a58b3868f205e7d59d2cfb40bcf344f4" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:47.958ex; height:7.176ex;"/>
        </span>

      <p>
       Obtaining
       <i>
        geodetic
       </i>
       latitude from
       <i>
        geocentric
       </i>
       coordinates from this relationship requires an iterative solution approach, otherwise the
       <i>
        geodetic
       </i>
       coordinates may be computed via the approach in the section above labeled "From ECEF to geodetic coordinates."
      </p>
      <p>
       The geocentric and geodetic longitude have the same value. This is true for the Earth and other similar shaped planets because their latitude lines (parallels) can be considered in much more degree perfect circles when compared to their longitude lines (meridians).
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \tan \lambda ={\frac {Y_{r}}{X_{r}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               tan
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ⁡
               <!-- ⁡ -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               λ
               <!-- λ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  Y
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   r
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  X
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   r
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \tan \lambda ={\frac {Y_{r}}{X_{r}}}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\tan \lambda ={\frac {Y_{r}}{X_{r}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3744528eb45249150691f8d09c7412bc44e6da42" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:11.935ex; height:5.676ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <b>
        Note:
       </b>
       Unambiguous determination of
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ \phi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mtext>
             </mtext>
             <mi>
              ϕ
              <!-- ϕ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \ \phi }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\ \phi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da404405931b4843facedeb034625cd306468e5c" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.966ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ \lambda }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mtext>
             </mtext>
             <mi>
              λ
              <!-- λ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \ \lambda }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\ \lambda " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2bfaa6ce1e7dfbb1b20e93a9cc5a7a1859bfeb67" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.936ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       requires knowledge of which
       <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinate_system#Two-dimensional_coordinate_system_quadrant" title="Cartesian coordinate system">
        quadrant
       </a>
       the coordinates lie in.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="From_ENU_to_ECEF">
        From ENU to ECEF
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [

        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: From ENU to ECEF">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       This is just the inversion of the ECEF to ENU transformation so
      </p>
      <dl>

        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conversion_across_map_projections">
        Conversion across map projections
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Conversion across map projections">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Conversion of coordinates and map positions among different map projections reference to the same datum may be accomplished either through direct translation formulas from one projection to another, or by first converting from a projection
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              A
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle A}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       to an intermediate coordinate system, such as ECEF, then converting from ECEF to projection
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              B
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle B}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/47136aad860d145f75f3eed3022df827cee94d7a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       . The formulas involved can be complex and in some cases, such as in the ECEF to geodetic conversion above, the conversion has no closed-form solution and approximate methods must be used. References such as the
       <i>
        DMA Technical Manual 8358.1
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TM8358.2_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TM8358.2-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the USGS paper
       <i>
        Map Projections: A Working Manual
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snyder1987_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Snyder1987-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       contain formulas for conversion of map projections. It is common to use computer programs to perform coordinate conversion tasks, such as with the DoD and NGA supported GEOTRANS program.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GEOTRANS_NGA_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GEOTRANS_NGA-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Datum_transformations">
        Datum transformations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Datum transformations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="floatright">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg" title="The different possible paths for transforming geographic coordinates from datum '&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000034-QINU`&quot;' to datum '&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000035-QINU`&quot;'">
        <img alt="coordinate transform paths" data-file-height="483" data-file-width="492" height="393" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg/400px-Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg/600px-Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg/800px-Possible_paths_for_datum_transform.svg.png 2x" width="400"/>
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Transformations among datums can be accomplished in a number of ways. There are transformations that directly convert geodetic coordinates from one datum to another. There are more indirect transforms that convert from geodetic coordinates to ECEF coordinates, transform the ECEF coordinates from one datum to the another, then transform ECEF coordinates of the new datum back to geodetic coordinates. There are also grid-based transformations that directly transform from one (datum, map projection) pair to another (datum, map projection) pair.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grid-based_method">
        Grid-based method
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Grid-based method">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="1115" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png/220px-Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png/330px-Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png/440px-Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Datum_Shift_Between_NAD27_and_NAD83.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Magnitude of shift in position between NAD27 and NAD83 datum as a function of location.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Grid-based transformations directly convert map coordinates from one (map-projection, geodetic datum) pair to map coordinates of another (map-projection, geodetic datum) pair. An example is the NADCON method for transforming from the North American Datum (NAD) 1927 to the NAD 1983 datum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESRI_grid_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ESRI_grid-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The High Accuracy Reference Network (HARN), a high accuracy version of the NADCON transforms, have an accuracy of approximately 5 centimeters. The National Transformation version 2 (
       <a href="/wiki/NTv2" title="NTv2">
        NTv2
       </a>
       ) is a Canadian version of NADCON for transforming between NAD 1927 and NAD 1983. HARNs are also known as NAD 83/91 and High Precision Grid Networks (HPGN).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nadcon_harn_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nadcon_harn-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Subsequently, Australia and New Zealand adopted the NTv2 format to create grid-based methods for transforming among their own local datums.
      </p>
      <p>
       Like the multiple regression equation transform, grid-based methods use a low-order interpolation method for converting map coordinates, but in two dimensions instead of three. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">
        NOAA
       </a>
       provides a software tool (as part of the NGS Geodetic Toolkit) for performing NADCON transformations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_NADCON_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_NADCON-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mulcare_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mulcare-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Molodensky_transformation">
        Molodensky transformation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Molodensky transformation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Molodensky transformation converts directly between geodetic coordinate systems of different datums without the intermediate step of converting to geocentric ECEF coordinates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esri_eq_based_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-esri_eq_based-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It requires the three shifts between the datum centers and the differences between the reference ellipsoid semi-major axes and flattening parameters.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Molodensky transform is used by the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Geospatial-Intelligence_Agency" title="National Geospatial-Intelligence Agency">
        National Geospatial-Intelligence Agency
       </a>
       (NGA) in their standard TR8350.2 and the NGA supported GEOTRANS program.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NGA_Datum_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NGA_Datum-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Molodensky method was popular before the advent of modern computers and the method is part of many geodetic programs.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Multiple_regression_equations">
        Multiple regression equations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Multiple regression equations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Datum transformations through the use of empirical
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_regression" title="Multiple regression">
        multiple regression
       </a>
       methods were created to achieve higher accuracy results over small geographic regions than the standard Molodensky transformations. MRE transforms are used to transform local datums over continent-sized or smaller regions to global datums, such as WGS 84.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IHO-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The standard NIMA TM 8350.2, Appendix D,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tr8350_2_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tr8350_2-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       lists MRE transforms from several local datums to WGS 84, with accuracies of about 2 meters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taylor_high_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-taylor_high-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The MREs are a direct transformation of geodetic coordinates with no intermediate ECEF step. Geodetic coordinates
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \phi _{B},\lambda _{B},h_{B}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               ϕ
               <!-- ϕ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                B
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               λ
               <!-- λ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                B
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               h
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                B
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

       </span>
       in the new datum
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

       are modeled as

       </span>
       . Given a sufficient number of
       <span class="mwe-math-element">

       </span>
       coordinate pairs for landmarks in both datums for good statistics, multiple regression methods are used to fit the parameters of these polynomials. The polynomials, along with the fitted coefficients, form the multiple regression equations.

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Helmert_transformation">
        Helmert transformation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Helmert transformation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Helmert_transformation" title="Helmert transformation">
        Helmert transformation
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Use of the Helmert transform in the transformation from geodetic coordinates of datum
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              A
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle A}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       to geodetic coordinates of datum
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              B
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle B}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/47136aad860d145f75f3eed3022df827cee94d7a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       occurs in the context of a three-step process:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HelmertNZ_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HelmertNZ-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Convert from geodetic coordinates to ECEF coordinates for datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

              </mi>

        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Apply the Helmert transform, with the appropriate
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle A\to B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>

             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

              </mo>
              <mi>

              </mi>

            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle A\to B}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="A\to B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5b8dd84619daff17b52a08b77d15db2b9ad6c2a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.121ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        transform parameters, to transform from datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>

              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle A}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        ECEF coordinates to datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

              </mi>

            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/47136aad860d145f75f3eed3022df827cee94d7a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        ECEF coordinates
       </li>
       <li>
        Convert from ECEF coordinates to geodetic coordinates for datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>

       In terms of ECEF XYZ vectors, the Helmert transform has the form

         <img alt="{\begin{bmatrix}X_{B}\\Y_{B}\\Z_{B}\end{bmatrix}}={\begin{bmatrix}c_{x}\\c_{y}\\c_{z}\end{bmatrix}}+(1+s\times 10^{-6})\cdot {\begin{bmatrix}1&amp;-r_{z}&amp;r_{y}\\r_{z}&amp;1&amp;-r_{x}\\-r_{y}&amp;r_{x}&amp;1\end{bmatrix}}\cdot {\begin{bmatrix}X_{A}\\Y_{A}\\Z_{A}\end{bmatrix}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2021f7c43a340eafabc24f9ec8c0a7bafe4d7804" style="vertical-align: -4.338ex; width:65.164ex; height:9.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The Helmert transform is a seven-parameter transform with three translation (shift) parameters
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{x},c_{y},c_{z}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                y
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                z
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle c_{x},c_{y},c_{z}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="c_{x},c_{y},c_{z}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9114309df3f90c0bdec98f19856ff3f5922ed25e" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.312ex; height:2.343ex;"/>
       </span>
       , three rotation parameters
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle r_{x},r_{y},r_{z}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                y
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                z
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle r_{x},r_{y},r_{z}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="r_{x},r_{y},r_{z}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9c32b2530cd4e81bdce43b0aab48beb71faed0c0" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.437ex; height:2.343ex;"/>
       </span>
       and one scaling (dilation) parameter
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle s}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              s
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle s}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="s" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01d131dfd7673938b947072a13a9744fe997e632" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       . The Helmert transform is an approximate method that is accurate when the transform parameters are small relative to the magnitudes of the ECEF vectors. Under these conditions, the transform is considered reversible.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OGP7_2_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OGP7_2-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A fourteen-parameter Helmert transform, with linear time dependence for each parameter,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OGP7_2_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-OGP7_2-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference nowrap">
        :
        <span>
         131-133
        </span>
       </sup>
       can be used to capture the time evolution of geographic coordinates dues to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geomorphic" title="Geomorphic">
        geomorphic
       </a>
       processes, such as continental drift.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolstad_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bolstad-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and earthquakes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-addend_8350_2_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-addend_8350_2-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This has been incorporated into software, such as the Horizontal Time Dependent Positioning (HTDP) tool from the U.S. NGS.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTDP_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HTDP-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Molodensky-Badekas_transformation">
        Molodensky-Badekas transformation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geographic_coordinate_conversion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Molodensky-Badekas transformation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       To eliminate the coupling between the rotations and translations of the Helmert transform, three additional parameters can be introduced to give a new XYZ center of rotation closer to coordinates being transformed. This ten-parameter model is called the
       <i>
        Molodensky-Badekas transformation
       </i>
       and should not be confused with the more basic Molodensky transform.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OGP7_2_25-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-OGP7_2-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference nowrap">
        :
        <span>
         133-134
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Like the Helmert transform, using the Molodensky-Badekas transform is a three-step process:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Convert from geodetic coordinates to ECEF coordinates for datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               A
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle A}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Apply the Molodensky-Badekas transform, with the appropriate
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle A\to B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               A
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               →
               <!-- → -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               B
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle A\to B}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="A\to B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5b8dd84619daff17b52a08b77d15db2b9ad6c2a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.121ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        transform parameters, to transform from datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               A
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle A}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        ECEF coordinates to datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>

              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="B" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/47136aad860d145f75f3eed3022df827cee94d7a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        ECEF coordinates
       </li>
       <li>
        Convert from ECEF coordinates to geodetic coordinates for datum
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle B}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

              </mi>

        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>

             {\displaystyle {\begin{bmatrix}X_{B}\\Y_{B}\\Z_{B}\end{bmatrix}}={\begin{bmatrix}X_{A}\\Y_{A}\\Z_{A}\end{bmatrix}}+{\begin{bmatrix}\Delta X_{A}\\\Delta Y_{A}\\\Delta Z_{A}\end{bmatrix}}+{\begin{bmatrix}1&amp;-r_{z}&amp;r_{y}\\r_{z}&amp;1&amp;-r_{x}\\-r_{y}&amp;r_{x}&amp;1\end{bmatrix}}\cdot {\begin{bmatrix}X_{A}-X_{A}^{0}\\Y_{A}-Y_{A}^{0}\\Z_{A}-Z_{A}^{0}\end{bmatrix}}+\Delta S{\begin{bmatrix}X_{A}-X_{A}^{0}\\Y_{A}-Y_{A}^{0}\\Z_{A}-Z_{A}^{0}\end{bmatrix}}.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
